116405589010408529617<//user_id>
<text>I am thrilled to see a new type of restaurant in Ojai!  This is exactly what Ojai needed.

The food is excellent the dining area is fun and vibrant the wine bar has a fantastic selection.

We enjoyed some wine and appetizers on the tables just outside the wine box (it’s the wine and beer).  We ordered way more appetizers then we needed to because we didn’t realize that the platter came with bread and we knew we had to try the bread!

We checked in a couple times to make sure they were not going to run out of chicken and we’re assured that if we ordered by eight it would be plenty. We ordered two full chickens,  a salad and four large sides and had way too much food for five people.   The sides that come with the chicken are very generous.

Our eyes were bigger than our stomachs but we want to make sure we were able to try a little bit of everything. I had read the reviews and had my list of dishes I wanted to try plus we overindulged on the bread because it was so delicious.

The leftovers were just as delicious if not better than they were the night before.

I wish Ojai Rotie the best of luck and look forward to returning soon!!< /text>< Time>

<user_id>108265770017021051223< /user_id><username>H< /username><time>1593411518426<//time><rating>5<//rating>< text>
The best courtyard/patio restaurant in Ojai. The roast chicken was phenomenal. The service was good. Good but cheap wine selection. We did not get the sourdough but I am guessing it would have been amazing with the juice chicken.

I went to Ojai Rotie during COVID season (end June) so I am assuming the service is even better during normal times. They served our food kinda takeout (in a bag, paper clothes and such) but they still served us wine and have our food in the lovely patio.</text>

Not sure what the deal is at this place. We walked into patio seating area, told we could sit anywhere and someone would be with us shortly. Noticed multiple other tables with people sitting, waiting. Wait staff just seemed to be walking around aimlessly, it appeared they were doing something, but it wasn’t grabbing menus, taking drink orders, or even bringing food out to people. After 10 minutes, and noticing that none of the other tables were being waited on we just decided to leave. It was surreal. I thought maybe at one point we were on a gotcha tv show, or part of a social experiment. Weird happenings in Ojai tonight.< /Text>

Wonderful spot in downtown. Great atmosphere, lovely wine selection, and tasty food. The casual vibe is refreshing. The food was good but a little disappointing for the price. <Text>Ojai Rotie catered our wedding in early October and our guests can’t stop talking about the food. Initially I was hesitant because at first glance the menu looked more like items for a picnic instead of a wedding.
But we changed our minds very quickly when we sat down for a tasting. Everything was of such high quality and superb taste that we immediately stopped looking elsewhere. The coleslaw is a perfect example. I’ve never been a big fan of coleslaw and usually found it to be pretty tasteless or full of mayonnaise. Larry and Claud’s creation however is so rich in flavor and freshness I’ve never had anything like it before. I can say pretty much the same for all the other items on the menu as well; they were all fantastic.
I was also concerned about replicating this quality at scale for a large wedding.  Have no fear. The food arrived fresh, hot and delicious and our guests gobbled it down. Oh, and the bread! That alone was worth the catering. Claud is a master baker and that homemade butter that accompanies his bread is like crack.
We can’t recommend Ojai Rotie enough. They worked tirelessly to make our big day one that even the foodies on our guest list raved about.< /Text><Time>1573781753312</Time>< Name>

<Review>Outstanding chicken! Tender and juicy. Went for the whole bird. I'll come back and try the half to see if it too is tender. Some could easily say the best chicken. This may have to be a weekly thing.

Sides we got (for take out) were the slaw and the cauliflower. Delicious. I think the slaw should be called kitchen sink slaw (jk) because there's everything but the kitchen sink in it. Heh. Never had coleslaw with jalepano peppers or peanuts before. There were even some golden raisins. My friend took a pass on it because it had a little cilantro in it. Heh.

The cauliflower was awesome. It had a curry taste (and must have been Turmeric based). So, extra stars for great sides that stand on their own.

Still full stars plus even though the bread wasn't a fav for me (this is personal pref. people love the bread). The chicken meal comes with a flat bread that's alright. We got a loaf of the sourdough too. The sourdough is certainly well made and has the perfect balance of crisp crust and soft center. For me though whole wheat sourdough isn't my deal. The wheat obscures the sourdough taste. I love a well made white sourdough.

Last note, this is mostly a patio dining (and I would think they do a lot of take away biz like we did) place. There's one café table inside but outside is where you want to sit. The walk up order counter is bizy.

We called ahead (which I think is a good idea for take away and easy). Just check your bag to make sure you got everything you ordered. (Poor girl forgot our sides. I think she felt worse about it than I did. They're busy so stuff like that happens now and then. )< /Review>< pics>
None</pics>

< review>
This place was amazing! The nurses, the receptionist, the surgeon! My first point of contact was Maria she is the one who sets everything up ,I think, she was great! Then I went in for different tests and the sleeping test, no complaints there either. Then surgery day comes, I check in with a really nice receptionist, get all prepped for surgery. I waited maybe 2-3 hours for my surgery which really isn't a big deal you are not waiting in the lobby area sitting down! I was in my bed getting prepped on my phone comfortable! My nurse for the day was Elena(I think that was her name it's kinda a blur) this girl is the best! She was soo nice so patient, I was asking a lot of questions. I can really say she was the one who made this the easiest/smoothest experience. Coming out of surgery I was in pain and she took real good care of me. She asked me if I was good enough to go home or if I wanted to stay the night, it was up to me. I chose to go home.This place is a 10/10 for me! One thing I think we should all remember is this is a tool, if you're not ready to be on a liquid diet for 4 weeks, eat smaller portions, and pretty much just be a healthier person you shouldn't be looking into VSG! The surgery is NOT the solution its just a tool that will help you reach your goal!</review>

<Text>After my gastric sleeve surgery I had absolutely no pain in my stomach. However I began vomiting often, was unable to start eating food, not even soft foods. As the weeks went by the vomiting continued and got more violent and happened more often. Oral meds for nausea/vomiting were not effective. Eventually I was admitted to Cedar-Sinai Hospital in Los Angeles where it was discovered that my esophagus had partially collapsed. I regret having the surgery. After the fact my surgeon told me that 1 out of 10 gastric sleeve surgersurgeries have serious complications! I am now going through the process of correcting this disaster and will update this when I am (hopefully) better. Please think hard before having this surgery. It's a nice tiny little neighborhood park.
I suggest stopping in to let the 5 North freeway traffic pass during Rush Hour.
You can grab a little bite to eat from any of the local eateries and bring it here to the park to relax and enjoy yourself before you head up to Santa Clarita or off the 14 freeway.
Just a suggestion.<//review>

<Text>ValleyCrest Telfair Park is a large rectangular park that is 3/4 open field with the remainder being a small playground and picnic area. The playground is a swing set and jungle gym in a sandbox. There are a few tables and a few coal-burning barbecues. There are no restrooms, no water fountains, no shade, and no parking lot. It’s not much of a destination but it is a good place to kick or throw balls if you’re local. The park is open from dawn until dusk.< /Text>< Rating>

< Text>
Nice place to camp, if a bit crowded. My son and I did RV camping here for the first time. They also offer tent camping with a few "boat in" campsites.

Most of the activities center around the reservoir. There is boating, swimming, jet skis and fishing. You can walk around the lake, but you're mostly on the side of a road, though there are a few embankments they aren't continuous.

Also, there is frequently a vendor onsite, but they are a temporary vendor (under a pavilion tent) and not necessarily always there so plan accordingly.

One nice touch is that there was an ice cream truck driving around.</Text>

Beware of spots with lack of shade trees.  Some parts of lake more like pond water then lake water.  Must bring in own firewood but Oakdale isnt far which is nice for ice runs.  Lots of bullfrogs at night and i mean all night making noise.  Showers are available.  Good family fun.  Lifetime memories made.  Been camping there for over 20 years and many memories were made there.<//review>

< Review>
Woodward reservoir a great place to go whether boating/tubing, jet sking, picnicking/bbq for the or camping for the weekend or the holiday. A very big day use area which usually get full. From day use areas to camping, Woodward has excellent swim areas for the kids all around the lake. RV full hook-up to camping and for larger camping groups the undeveloped camping area is a excellent place to set up camp. Be aware of the speed limit inside the park as there are Sheriff's patrolling and WILL ticket speeders, their presence is noticeable but they do not bother you at your campsite. Dogs are allowed but must be leashed. Horseback riding is also allowed. A great place for the kids to swim and enjoy themselves< /Review>

I drove around for 20 minutes looking for mine. And it's all dirt roads, some deeply rutted or up large hills that you can't see over until you get over the top and start down the other side. A few camp sites are for reservations, the rest are first come, first serve. I had a nice camp site picked out until a group of people took the spot next to mine and proceeded to blast mariachi music at full volume. Luckily the spots aren't reserved so I just moved to the other side of the lake, where there were 2 camps near by blasting mariachi music until 1:30 am. I showed my displeasure by making very loud breakfast the next morning at 5:30. It's $20 a night to camp, so bring cash. Most of the camp sites are right on the water, my tent was about 10 feet from the bank and I woke up to my tent surrounded by geese, which was amazing. Bathrooms are more like outhouses, but almost always have toilet paper... Though I still bring a few rolls just in case. They have little fire pit BBQs which are good for s'mores or meals. Woodward employees are great. The park and campsites we're good. Just keep in mind during summer operation, grass is very limited so you have to deal with dirt or hay for ground cover. < review>
Too many mexicans dominate and continually occupy the best camp sites. (They keep using family members names to rent those sites continuously all year round. They put toilet paper beside, instead of in, the toilets. Play music too loud and until late at night. Park rangers seem afraid to stand up to them. They (a lot of, but not all) leave garbage everywhere. Dont leave their campsites clean. Day use people occupy campsites. That means campers can't get a good site until the day users leave around 10pm. I loved the reservoir growing up. But now its like Mexico has moved in and taken over. I don't think its safe for children and teenagers. I'm not prejudiced. But these have been my experiences.</review>
